<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-indent: -0.5in; text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 18pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino; color: #ffffff; background-color: #808080;"><b><span style="line-height: 115%;">Spiritual Message for the Day  Place Yourself In Your Real Self by Sri Swami Padmanabhanandaji</span></b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-indent: -0.5in; text-align: center;">&nbsp;<strong style="text-indent: -0.5in;"><span style="font-family: book antiqua,palatino; font-size: 12pt; color: #3366ff;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"><span style="color: #0000ff;">Baba Times Digest | 18 November 2015 14</span></span></span></strong><strong style="text-indent: -0.5in;"><span style="font-family: book antiqua,palatino; font-size: 12pt; color: #3366ff;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"><span style="color: #0000ff;">.59 EST | New York Edition</span></span></span></strong></p>
<hr />
<div>
<table cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" hspace="0" vspace="0" align="left">
<tbody>
<tr>
<td valign="top" align="left" style="padding-top: 0in; padding-right: 9.0pt; padding-bottom: 0in; padding-left: 9.0pt;">
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b>Place Yourself In Your Real Self<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b>Divine Life Society Publication: Online meditation &amp; Satsang via Skype by Sri Swami Padmanabhanandaji<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b>(Spoken on November 15,2015 via Skype to Bhagavadgita Study group  Australia, New Zealand, USA)<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b><span style="text-decoration: underline;"><span style="color: red;"><a href="https://www.dropbox.com/l/s/DGWqJClVTSaf8xhrUkAWKr"><span style="color: #0000ff;"><span style="color: #0000ff;">AUDIO LINK FOR THIS SPEECH</span></span></a><o:p></o:p></span></span></b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">I am happy to be here to meet you all and to participate in this Satsang via Skype especially the study group those who are studying Gita and the transit from the third chapter to the fourth chapter.</span><o:p></o:p></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">I will give an outline of what you have studied so far. </span><o:p></o:p></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">The first chapter of Bhagavadgita is the chapter of delusion.&nbsp; The Sastras declare that we are basically divine. You are not this mortal being. We are immortal, changeless immortal. Everlasting peace and happiness is our nature but unfortunately we are not aware of it.</span><o:p></o:p></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">This non-awareness of our real self and in that place awareness of a wrong person and another self which is full of problems, facing miseries in life, so that condition is created by an agent we call it as <i>moha</i>.&nbsp; Arjuna was under the grip of <i>moha</i> because of that <i>moha</i> he had <i>shoka</i>. <i>Moha</i> is delusion and because of the delusion he has sorrow in life. Because of this <i>moha</i> we are under the grip of shoka. <i>Shoka</i> means sorrow. To overcome that Bhagavan says in the second chapter which according to Sankaracharya &nbsp;is the beginning of the Bhagavadgita. The first chapter, he says is only an introduction, a presentation of what the situation is like.</span><o:p></o:p></p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">So in the second chapter Bhagawan says: <i>Ashochyaan anvashochastwam prajnaavaadaamshcha bhaashase; Gataasoon agataasoomshcha naanushochanti panditaah.</i>(2.11)<o:p></o:p></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Bhagavan says, what is this worrying about a thing about which you should not be worried at all. </span><o:p></o:p></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">&nbsp;The real Gita begins from that <i>slokha</i> (verse). To overcome that <i>shoka</i>, to overcome that grief, and to overcome that pain we are undergoing in life, the delusion we are having, what is needed is discrimination. Knowledge is needed. So, in the second chapter Bhagavan goes on to speak about our imperishable nature. Your nature is full of <i>Ananda</i>. Your nature is <i>Sat-chid-ananda</i> <i>svarupa</i>. You are not this body, nor this mind, and all this thoughts you are entertaining are not your real thoughts. They are the creations of the mind. The mind makes you feel like that. So you go beyond the mind. </span><o:p></o:p></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Keep your position, yourself, in your real Self. You shall be your real Self. That is achieved through discrimination, through understanding. So, the second chapter deals with the discrimination  <i>Jnana</i>. Bhagavan speaks about this and gives the nature of the person - one who is established in the real Self.&nbsp; He is called <i>stitha prajna</i>. He is established in the real Self. And what are his qualities, how he will look like, how he will behave, are told in the end of the second chapter. So the second chapter concludes here.</span><o:p></o:p></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Bhagavan says to Arjuna, understand that you need knowledge; Supreme knowledge so you can place yourself in your Real Self and thereafter there is no shoka. There is no delusion. There is no sorrow. </span><o:p></o:p></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Then in that case I will go to Himalayas, go to Sivananda Ashram, have a room there and enjoy food and remain there. I will not do any work, like that people begin to think. Then Bhagavan says, No, No, it is not correct. You have to do your activities also. With this knowledge you should place yourself in that condition and carry on all activities. Place yourself in your Real Self and carry on all your duties  worldly duties. Because you are here in this world, you cannot neglect this. You have to do all your activities here. While you are doing all your activities here, you should place yourself in the original nature that is what he says. </span><o:p></o:p></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Suppose a person is acting in the drama as a villain and his own brother or son or somebody close to him is the hero. While he is fighting with the hero, he knows very well that it is only a drama, it is only acting. That is the requirement of the stage. In reality our relationship is different. Likewise you should be aware of your real nature and carry on with the activities of this world. He explains that as Yajna.</span><o:p></o:p></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Yajna means you have to do your duties in this world and while you are performing your duties you must also place yourself in your real position (Self).</span><o:p></o:p></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Do not identify with the mind. Do not identify with the desire. Do not identify with your intellectual concepts. Identify with your real self and discharge your duties as it comes before you. Then that is what is called the Yajna. It is called Karma Yoga. That has been explained in the third chapter.</span><o:p></o:p></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Now in the fourth chapter, &nbsp;Bhagavan says that this knowledge although I have told you and you keep on contemplating on that, you forget and you get deluded due to the flux (continuous change) and every time I shall re-establish this. People understand but in the course of time again they are deluded and then I have to come back here again to reestablish he says.</span><o:p></o:p></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">So Bhagavan says that he has to come back again and again whenever it is needed. A bulb which is glowing collects dust. Every week you wipe it and make it clean, as you wash your clothes, as you wash your room and the walls again and again to make it clean. Because of the constant contact with the outer world, it gets dirty. Clean it up again and make it look clean and neat. Likewise this also has to be done. For that, I, again and again take this <i>avatara</i> and re-establish this truth. That is the fourth chapter. </span><o:p></o:p></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Hari om.</span><o:p></o:p></p>
<p align="center" style="margin: 0in 0in 0.0001pt; text-align: center; background-image: initial; background-attachment: initial; background-size: initial; background-origin: initial; background-clip: initial; background-position: initial; background-repeat: initial;">&nbsp;</p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b>Audio link and download</b>: </span><b><span style="font-size: 9.0pt;"><a href="https://www.dropbox.com/l/s/DGWqJClVTSaf8xhrUkAWKr"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino; color: #0000ff;"><span style="color: #0000ff;">Place Yourself In Your Real Self by Sri Swami Padmanabhanandaji</span></span></a><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</div>
